## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the instantaneous population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population P, which is the core of ordinary differential equation models in population ecology. Classical models typically formulate dP/dt as an autonomous function of P (e.g., exponential, logistic, Allee) or a non-autonomous function including explicit time dependence (e.g., seasonal forcing, time-varying carrying capacity).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited Malthusian growth)
- Logistic growth (parabolic): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (self-limiting growth, c1 < 0)
- Generalized logistic/Bertalanffy: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P**c3 (allometric growth and mortality)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (or c0 * P + c1 * P * log(P), typical in tumor or economic growth with decreasing relative rate)
- Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic form allowing negative growth below a threshold)
- Constant harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 (additive constant harvest rate, c2 < 0)
- Density-dependent saturation mortality (Holling type II): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 / (c2 + P) (saturating death rate at high density)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environmental fluctuations affecting growth rate)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * t)) (linearly changing habitat capacity)
- Beverton–Holt type differential: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + P) - c2 * P (contest competition birth with constant mortality)
- Logistic with sinusoidal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) * P (separable time–density effects)
- Gompertz with linear time trend: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P * log(c2 * P) (accelerating or decelerating relative growth rate over time)
- Threshold harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 * max(0, P - c3) (harvest only when population exceeds safe limit)
- Carrying capacity exponential shift: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * t))) (habitat degradation or restoration)
- Power-law multiplicative time effect: dP_dt = c0 * t**c1 * P + c2 * P**c3 (non-stationary scaling of growth and mortality with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Self-limiting (logistic) feedback → negative quadratic or higher‑power term in P dominates at large P
- Allee / critical depensation → growth rate becomes negative at low P, requiring a cubic polynomial or product form with a sign change
- Seasonal or periodic environment → oscillatory functions of t (sine, cosine) multiplied by P or added to growth rate
- Constant‑effort harvesting or background mortality → additive constant term independent of P (often negative)
- Density‑dependent mortality saturation → rational form P²/(c+P) captures diminishing returns of mortality at high density
- Gompertz / resource exhaustion → per‑capita growth rate linear in log(P) drives a log(P) factor in dP/dt
- Time‑varying capacity → P is divided by a non‑constant function of t, yielding mixed polynomial‑rational forms
- Threshold management → piecewise functions like max(0, P‑c) appear when harvesting/control only starts above a threshold
- Boom‑bust cycles → product of P and a periodic t‑function generates oscillatory growth curves
- Allometric scaling → power‑law terms P**c with non‑integer exponents describe size‑dependent metabolism or birth/death

"P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P**2*c5 + P*c6", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + c3*t*(P + c4)**c5", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5*(c6 + t)**c7 + P*c8", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8 + c9*t) + 1)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(P*c8 + c9)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*t + c9))", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*t) + P*c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(P*c7 + 1) + c8)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*sin(P*c7 + c8)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*t) + 1)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)", "P**2*c0/(c1 + c2*t) + P*c3 + P**c4*c5*t**c6 + c7", "P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*t**c7", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3*t**c4", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**(1/3)*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P + c3)**c4", "P**(1/3)*c0/(c1 + c2*t) + P**(1/3)*c3*t/(c1 + c2*t) + P**2*c4/(c1 + c2*t) + P*c5/(c1 + c2*t) + P*c6*t/(c1 + c2*t)", "P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1/(c2 + c3*t) + P*c4 + c5*t*(P + c6)**c7"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
`-c0*c1*P + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P^c6 + c7*P`

Substituting values:
- `-6.2168 * 1.4128 * P = -8.7834 * P`
- `0.8579 * (1 - P/79.2026) * P = 0.8579*P - 0.01083*P²`
- `0.8579 * P^(1/3)`
- `0.8579 * P`

Combining: `P^(1/3) * 0.8579 + P * (-8.7834 + 0.8579 + 0.8579) + P² * (-0.01083)`

So GT = `0.8579 * P^(1/3) - 7.0676 * P - 0.01083 * P²`

This is: **P^(1/3) * c + P * c' + P² * c''** — a function of P only (no t dependence).

The GT has three basis functions: `P^(1/3)`, `P`, and `P²`.

Now I'll check each candidate for the ability to reduce to this form.

For a candidate to match, it must:
1. Have exactly the basis functions P^(1/3), P, and P² (or equivalent)
2. No t-dependence that can't be eliminated
3. No other non-eliminable basis functions (sin, exp, log, etc.)

Let me systematically go through candidates, focusing on structure:

**Candidates that are clearly `P^(1/3) + P² + P + constant terms` (no t, no transcendental):**

**Candidate 104**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3`
Set c3=0: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2`. This matches GT! ✓

**Candidate 118**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2`
Directly matches GT! ✓

**Candidate 103**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P^(1/3)*c1 + P²*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4 + c5`
= `P^(1/3)*(c0+c1) + P²*c2 + P*(c3+c4) + c5`. Set c5=0: matches GT! ✓

**Candidate 117**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P^(1/3)*c1 + P²*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4`
= `P^(1/3)*(c0+c1) + P²*c2 + P*(c3+c4)`. Matches GT! ✓

Now let me check candidates with t-dependence that might be eliminable:

**Candidates with `P²/(c + c*exp(c*t))` terms**: These have t-dependence in the P² coefficient that cannot be eliminated (setting c4=0 or c3=0 would make it P²*c1/c2 which is just P²*const, but we need to check if the remaining terms work).

For candidates like **71**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5`
If c4=0: `P²*c1/(c2+c3) + ...` = constant * P². This works! Matches GT! ✓

Similarly **102**: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6`. Set c4=0, c6=0: matches! ✓

**Candidate 53**: Same as 102 with P*c6+P*c8 = P*(c6+c8). Set c4=0: matches! ✓

Let me now systematically check all candidates. I'll group them:

**Group: P^(1/3) + P² + P (pure polynomial in P, no t)**

- **104**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3 → set c3=0 → MATCH ✓
- **118**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 → MATCH ✓
- **103**: MATCH ✓ (as shown)
- **117**: MATCH ✓ (as shown)

**Group: P^(1/3) + P²/(c+c*exp(ct)) + P + ...** where t can be eliminated:

- **71**: set c4=0 → P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3) + P*c5 → MATCH ✓
- **102**: set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **53**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + P*c6 + c7. Set c4=0, c7=0 → MATCH ✓
- **52**: + c6*t + c7. Set c4=0, c6=0, c7=0 → MATCH ✓
- **70**: + c6*log(c7*t+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **96**: + c6*sin(c7*t+c8). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **97**: + c6*exp(c7*t). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **74**: + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*t+c9)). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **95**: + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*t)+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **112**: + c6*t^c7. Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **108**: + P*c6*t^c7. Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **110**: + P*c6*sin(c7*t+c8). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **40**: + P*c6/(c7+c8*exp(c9*t)). Set c4=0, c9=0 → P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*const + P*c5 + P*c6/(c7+c8) → MATCH ✓
- **46**: + P^c6*c7. Set c4=0. Then P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*const + P*c5 + P^c6*c7. Need c6 to be 1/3 or 1 or 2 or set c7=0. Set c7=0 → MATCH ✓
- **57**: + P*c6/(P+c7). This adds P*c6/(P+c7) which is a rational function of P, not polynomial. Set c6=0 → MATCH ✓ (with c4=0)
- **62**: + P*c6*log(P*c7+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **42**: + P^c6*c7*log(P*c8+1). Set c4=0, c7=0 → MATCH ✓
- **48**: + c6*exp(P*c7). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **88**: + c6*sin(P*c7+c8). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **44**: + c6*exp(c7*sin(P*c8+c9)). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **72**: + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8+c9*t)+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **73**: + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(P*c8+c9). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **36**: + c6*log(P*c7+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **24**: + c6*exp(c7*t)*log(P*c8+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **61**: + c6*t*(P+c7)^c8. Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **55**: + c6*t^c7*Max(0,P+c8). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **69**: + P*c6*t*log(P*c7+1). Set c4=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **68**: + P*c5*(c6+t)^c7 + P*c8. Set c4=0, c7=0 → P*c5*c6^0 + P*c8 = P*(c5+c8). Wait, c7=0 means (c6+t)^0=1, so P*c5 + P*c8. Combined with P*c5 already... Actually the formula is P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5*(c6+t)^c7 + P*c8. Set c4=0, c7=0: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*const + P*c5 + P*c8 → MATCH ✓
- **63**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2/(c3+c4*exp(c5*t)) + P*c6. Set c5=0, c1=0 → MATCH ✓
- **66**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*exp(c4*t)) + P²*c5 + P*c6. Set c4=0 → P²*(c1/(c2+c3)+c5) + ... → MATCH ✓

**Group: Candidates with `P²/(c+c*t)` terms:**
- **25**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*t) + P*c4 + c5 + c6*exp(c7*sin(P*c8+c9)). Set c3=0, c5=0, c6=0 → MATCH ✓
- **85**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*t) + P*c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(P*c7+1)+c8). Set c3=0, c5=0 → MATCH ✓
- **133**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*t) + P*c4 + c5*t*(P+c6)^c7. Set c3=0, c5=0 → MATCH ✓

**Group: Candidates with `P²*c1/(P+c2)` terms:**
This gives P²/(P+c) = P - c + c²/(P+c), which introduces a 1/(P+c) term. Not polynomial.
- **17**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(P*c7+c8)). Set c5=0, c4=0: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3. P²/(P+c2) = P - c2 + c2²/(P+c2). This is NOT a polynomial. But we can set c1=0 → P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c3. Missing P². NO MATCH ✗
- **59**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(P*c6+1)+c7). Set c4=0, c1=0 → missing P². NO MATCH ✗

Wait, for 17: we can't get P² from P²/(P+c2) alone. But if c2=0: P²*c1/P = c1*P. Then we just have P^(1/3)*c0 + c1*P + P*c3 = P^(1/3)*c0 + P*(c1+c3). Missing P². NO MATCH ✗

Actually wait - for candidate 59, set c2=0: P²*c1/P = c1*P. Still missing P². Set c4=0: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3. We need this to equal P^(1/3)*a + P*b + P²*d. P²/(P+c2) is not a polynomial unless c2=0, in which case it becomes P. So NO MATCH.

**Group: P + P^c + constant (no P^(1/3) explicit):**
- **105**: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4. Set c2=1/3, c4=0 → MATCH ✓
- **106**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4. Set c2=2, c4=0 → MATCH ✓
- **119**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3. Set c2=2 → MATCH ✓
- **41**: P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + P^c3*c4 + c5. Set c1=1/3, c3=2, c5=0 → MATCH ✓
- **30**: P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(P*c6+c7)). Set c1=1/3, c4=0, c3=0. Missing P². NO MATCH ✗

Wait, candidate 30: P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(P*c6+c7)). Set c4=0, c3=0: P*c0 + P^c1*c2. Only two basis functions. Need P^(1/3), P, P². Can set c1=1/3 but then missing P². Or c1=2 but missing P^(1/3). NO MATCH ✗

- **128**: P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(P*c5). Set c4=0, c3=0, c1=1/3: missing P². NO MATCH ✗
- **43**: P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*log(P^c5*c6+1). Set c4=0, c3=0: same issue. NO MATCH ✗

**Group: P^(1/3) + P + P^c + extras:**
- **120**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P+c3)^c4. If c4=2, c3=0: c2*P². → P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*P² → MATCH ✓
- **90**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P*c3+1)^c4 + c5. If c4=2: c2*(c3*P+1)² = c2*c3²*P² + 2*c2*c3*P + c2. Then total: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*(c1+2*c2*c3) + c2*c3²*P² + (c2+c5). Set c2+c5=0 (i.e., c5=-c2). Then we get P^(1/3)*c0 + P*(c1+2*c2*c3) + c2*c3²*P². This works! MATCH ✓

**Group: Candidates with sin, cos, log, exp of P that can't be zeroed:**
Many candidates have terms like `sin(c*log(P*c+1)+c)` or `exp(c*sin(P*c+c))`. These can be set to zero by setting their coefficient to 0.

Let me check candidates with such terms where the coefficient CAN be set to 0:

- **77**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(P*c4+1)+c5). Set c2=0: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1. Missing P². NO MATCH ✗
- **131**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(P*c4+1)+c5) + c6. Set c2=0, c6=0: missing P². NO MATCH ✗
- **39**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(P*c5+c6)). Set c3=0, c2=0: missing P². NO MATCH ✗

For these candidates without a P² term and no way to generate one, they can't match.

**Candidate 9**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(P*c6+1)+c7). Set c2=2, c4=0 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 12**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(P*c7+c8)). Set c2=2, c4=0, c5=0 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 13**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P+c3) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(P*c7+c8)). Set c5=0, c4=0, c2=0: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1. Missing P². NO MATCH ✗

Wait, P*c2/(P+c3) - can this generate P²? No, it's a rational function. Set c2=0 to eliminate it. Then missing P². NO MATCH ✗

**Candidate 107**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*t*(P+c5)^c6. Set c4=0, c2=2 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 114**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3*t^c4. Set c4=0, c2=2 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 45**: P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + P^c3*c4*t^c5 + c6. Set c5=0, c1=1/3, c3=2, c6=0 → P*c0 + P^(1/3)*c2 + P²*c4 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 47**: P*c0 + P*c1*log(P*c2+1) + P^c3*c4*t^c5 + c6. Set c1=0, c5=0, c3=1/3, c6=0: P*c0 + P^(1/3)*c4. Missing P². Or c3=2: P*c0 + P²*c4. Missing P^(1/3). NO MATCH ✗

Wait, we have P*c0 + P*c1*log(P*c2+1) + P^c3*c4*t^c5 + c6. Set c1=0, c5=0: P*c0 + P^c3*c4 + c6. Only two free basis functions (P and P^c3). Can set c3=1/3 but then missing P², or c3=2 but missing P^(1/3). NO MATCH ✗

**Candidate 99**: P²*c0/(c1+c2*t) + P*c3 + P^c4*c5*t^c6 + c7. Set c2=0, c6=0, c4=1/3, c7=0: P²*c0/c1 + P*c3 + P^(1/3)*c5 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 100**: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5. Set c4=0, c2=1/3, c5=0 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 101**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5. Set c4=0, c2=2, c5=0 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 115**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P²*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4. Set c2=0 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 116**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3. Set c2=0 → MATCH ✓

**Candidate 65**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3/(c4+c5*exp(c6*t)). Set c6=0: P*c3/(c4+c5). Combined with P*c2 → P*(c2+c3/(c4+c5)). → MATCH ✓

Now let me go through remaining candidates more carefully:

**Candidate 1**: P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1/(c2+c3*exp(c4*t)) + P*c5 + c6*t/(P*c7+c8) + c9/(P*c7+c8). Set c4=0, c6=0, c9=0 (or c7=0 and then c9/c8 is constant, set to 0): → MATCH ✓ (set c4=0, c7=0, c6=0, c9=0 → P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*const + P*c5)
